## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations
**Analysis**: The task models acceleration dv/dt in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, with inputs time t and velocity v. In such systems, acceleration often depends only on v via energy conservation (e.g., a = ±√(E − ½v²)) or includes t when external driving is present. The absence of displacement x suggests an autonomous first-order ODE dv/dt = f(v) or a non‑autonomous one with explicit time forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- SHM energy conservation: dv_dt = c0 * sqrt(c1 - c2 * v**2)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v
- Cubic damping (nonlinear friction): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v**3
- Rayleigh self-sustained oscillation: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3
- Duffing energy relation: dv_dt = c0 * sqrt(c1 - v**2) + c2 * (c1 - v**2)**(3/2)
- Forced harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c2 * t)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * v * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t))
- Power‑law damping: dv_dt = -c0 * Abs(v)**c1 * sign(v)
- Saturating damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v / (1 + c1 * Abs(v))
- Relativistic oscillator limit: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - (v / c1)**2)**c2
- Exponential damping with time modulation: dv_dt = -c0 * v * exp(c1 * t)
- Generalized restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 - v**2)**c2 * sign(v)
- Mixed forcing and damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)
- Amplitude‑dependent frequency (nonlinear spring): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v * Abs(v)**c2
- Threshold‑activated damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v * (1 - c1 / (1 + c2 * v**2))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Even‑symmetry in acceleration vs. velocity (e.g., square‑root of (C − v²)) indicates energy conservation in a potential well.
- Odd‑power damping terms (v, v³, v⁵) represent dissipative forces typical of mechanical friction or fluid drag.
- A positive linear damping coefficient with a negative cubic term (c0*v - c1*v³) signals a self‑sustained oscillator (e.g., van der Pol type).
- Explicit periodic functions of t (cos, sin) in the acceleration expression imply external driving or parametric forcing.
- Square‑root or fractional‑power functions of v suggest the oscillator’s phase curve is an ellipse or a higher‑order oval (constant energy contours).
- The appearance of (1 − (v/c)²) or similar saturating factors indicates a limiting speed (relativistic or finite‑energy bound).
- If dv/dt contains only odd functions of v and no explicit t, the system is likely autonomous and energy‑conservative or purely dissipative.
- Coupling between v and exponential/trigonometric functions of t points to Floquet‑type or parametrically excited systems.
- Rational forms like v/(1 + |v|) approximate smooth Coulomb dry friction or saturation in damping mechanisms.
- Acceleration proportional to v times a power of |v| (|v|^p * v) appears in nonlinear drag laws (e.g., quadratic drag p=1, high‑Reynolds flow).

### Candidate 1: c0*v + c1*cos(c2*t + c3) + c4*v*cos(c5*t) + c6*sin(c7*v + c8)*cos(c9*t)

With c3=-π/2: c1*sin(t) + c6*sin(v). This works!
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: c0*v + c1*cos(c2*t+c3) + c4*sin(c5*v+c6) + c7*v/(c8*v+c9)
Set c0=0. The term c7*v/(c8*v+c9) is a rational function of v. If c7=0, we get c1*cos(c2*t+c3) + c4*sin(c5*v+c6). Set c2=1, c3=-π/2, c5=1, c6=0: sin(t) + c4*sin(v). Works!

### Candidate 4: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*sin(c3*t+c4) + c5*sin(c6*t+c7)*cos(c8*v+c9)
Set c0=0. The last term mixes t and v. Set c5=0: c1*cos(t) + c2*sin(c3*t+c4). This gives only functions of t, no sin(v). Can't match GT.
Alternatively, keep c5≠0. sin(c6*t+c7)*cos(c8*v+c9) = product of trig functions. Using product-to-sum: this gives sin(c6*t+c7+c8*v+c9) + sin(c6*t+c7-c8*v-c9), which are mixed terms. We need pure sin(v) which requires c6=0: then sin(c7)*cos(c8*v+c9) = constant*cos(c8*v+c9). With c8=1, c9=-π/2: constant*sin(v). And c1*cos(t)+c2*sin(c3*t+c4) can give sin(t). Set c3=1, c4=0, c1=0 or combine. Yes, this works!
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: c0*v + c1*cos(c2*t+c3) + c4*v*cos(c5*t) + c6*cos(c7*v+c8*exp(c9*t))

Actually if c8=0 exactly, cos(c7*v) with appropriate c7 and c6 can give -sin(v)? cos(v) = sin(v+π/2). We need sin(v), which is cos(v-π/2). But there's no additive phase constant for v.
